<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kendrick Lamar Duckworth</b> (born June 17, 1987) is an American rapper and songwriter. Known for his <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rap" title="Progressive rap">progressive</a> musical styles and <a href="/wiki/Social_consciousness" title="Social consciousness">socially conscious</a> songwriting, he is considered one of the most influential hip hop artists of his generation and one of the greatest rappers of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a>, Lamar began his career as a teenager performing under the stage name K.Dot. He quickly garnered local attention which led to him signing a recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Top_Dawg_Entertainment" title="Top Dawg Entertainment">Top Dawg Entertainment</a> (TDE) in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After becoming a founding member of the hip hop supergroup <a href="/wiki/Black_Hippy" title="Black Hippy">Black Hippy</a>, Lamar dropped his former stage name of <b>K.Dot</b> and started using his first and middle names professionally. In 2011, he released his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Section.80" title="Section.80">Section.80</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Political_hip_hop#Conscious_hip_hop" title="Political hip hop">conscious hip hop</a> record. The album was met with positive reviews and included his debut single "<a href="/wiki/HiiiPoWeR" title="HiiiPoWeR">HiiiiPower</a>". In 2012, Lamar secured a record deal with <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>, under the aegis of <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, and released his second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Kid,_M.A.A.D_City" title="Good Kid, M.A.A.D City">Good Kid, M.A.A.D City</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> influenced album garnered widespread critical recognition and commercial success, while including the singles "<a href="/wiki/Swimming_Pools_(Drank)" title="Swimming Pools (Drank)">Swimming Pools (Drank)</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Backseat_Freestyle" title="Backseat Freestyle">Backseat Freestyle</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Bitch,_Don%27t_Kill_My_Vibe" title="Bitch, Don&#39;t Kill My Vibe">Bitch, Don't Kill My Vibe</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A visit to South Africa inspired Lamar's <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>-flavored third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/To_Pimp_a_Butterfly" title="To Pimp a Butterfly">To Pimp a Butterfly</a></i> (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It received universal acclaim and became his first number-one album on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The same year, he topped the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for the first time with the remix of "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Blood_(Taylor_Swift_song)" title="Bad Blood (Taylor Swift song)">Bad Blood</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Lamar experimented with <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_soul" title="Psychedelic soul">psychedelic soul</a> in his fourth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Damn_(Kendrick_Lamar_album)" title="Damn (Kendrick Lamar album)">Damn</a></i> (2017). It spawned his first solo number-one single "<a href="/wiki/Humble_(song)" title="Humble (song)">Humble</a>" and became the first non-classical and non-jazz work to be awarded the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Music" title="Pulitzer Prize for Music">Pulitzer Prize for Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Following a four-year hiatus, Lamar released his fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Morale_%26_the_Big_Steppers" title="Mr. Morale &amp; the Big Steppers">Mr. Morale &amp; the Big Steppers</a></i> (2022), which served as his <a href="/wiki/Swan_song" title="Swan song">swan song</a> from TDE.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He has directed and produced several music videos and films with his creative partner <a href="/wiki/Dave_Free" title="Dave Free">Dave Free</a>, with whom he founded the creative collective <a href="/wiki/PGLang" title="PGLang">PGLang</a>.
</p><p>Having sold over 70 million records in the United States alone, all of Lamar's studio albums have been <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_certification" title="Music recording certification">certified platinum</a> or higher by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He has received <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Kendrick_Lamar" title="List of awards and nominations received by Kendrick Lamar">numerous accolades</a> throughout his career, including 17 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime Emmy Award</a>, two <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, 11 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a>, and a nomination for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a>. He was named <a href="/wiki/MTV%27s_Hottest_MCs_in_the_Game" title="MTV&#39;s Hottest MCs in the Game">MTV's Hottest MC in the Game</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Lamar received the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Senate" title="California State Senate">California State Senate</a>'s Generational Icon Award. He has been featured in listicles such as the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100"><i>Time</i> 100</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forbes_30_Under_30" title="Forbes 30 Under 30"><i>Forbes</i> 30 Under 30</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-time_100_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_100-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Three of his studio albums were included on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s 2020 ranking of the <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone&#39;s 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Kendrick Lamar Duckworth was born on June 17, 1987, in <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a>, to Paula Oliver, a <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> worker, and Kenneth "Kenny" Duckworth, a <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a> worker.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> His parents were from the <a href="/wiki/South_Side,_Chicago" title="South Side, Chicago">South Side of Chicago</a> and relocated to Compton three years before his birth due to his father's affiliation with the <a href="/wiki/Gangster_Disciples" title="Gangster Disciples">Gangster Disciples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Lamar is the eldest of four children and was named after singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Kendricks" title="Eddie Kendricks">Eddie Kendricks</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Temptations" title="The Temptations">the Temptations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He was raised in a <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a> <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African American</a> family, lived in <a href="/wiki/Section_8_(housing)" title="Section 8 (housing)">Section 8</a> housing, and was reliant on <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">welfare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Although he wasn't a member of a gang, he grew up among close affiliates of the <a href="/wiki/Bloods" title="Bloods">Westside Piru Bloods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eells_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eells-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lamar developed an interest in music when he was four years old after listening to the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> records his parents would play at their house parties.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenburg_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenburg-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Some of his earliest childhood memories included watching his father and uncles rob stores during the <a href="/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_riots" title="1992 Los Angeles riots">1992 Los Angeles riots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eells_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eells-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He credits the riots for giving him a better understanding of <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a> after learning about the <a href="/wiki/Rodney_King" title="Rodney King">beating of Rodney King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eells_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eells-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He was given the nickname "Man-Man" as a child because he carried himself as an adult.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This nickname would later be used as a reference to his childhood in <a href="/wiki/Humble_(song)" title="Humble (song)">HUMBLE.</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Family_Ties_(song)" title="Family Ties (song)">Family Ties</a>. When he was five years old, Lamar witnessed his first murder while sitting outside of his apartment unit. He admitted during an interview with <a href="/wiki/NPR_Music" title="NPR Music">NPR Music</a> that it "done something to me right then and there. It let me know that this is not only something that I'm looking at, but it's something that maybe I have to get used to."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Three years later, he witnessed his second murder as he was walking home from Ronald E. McNair Elementary School.<sup id="cite_ref-Eells_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eells-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When he was eight years old, Lamar saw rappers <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> film the music video for their single "<a href="/wiki/California_Love" title="California Love">California Love</a>" in his neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The experience inspired him to pursue a recording career and he began <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyling</a> soon after.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenburg_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenburg-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He described himself as being quiet, shy, and observant in school; his mother stated that he was a <a href="/wiki/Loner" title="Loner">loner</a> until the age of seven.<sup id="cite_ref-Eells_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eells-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> When he was a seventh-grade student at Vanguard Learning Center, Lamar was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a> by his English teacher Regis Inge, who connected the literary form to hip hop.<sup id="cite_ref-Nation_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The class had a notable impact on him; as it opened up "an avenue to unpack his feelings" and "helped him navigate the social dynamics of his neighborhood."<sup id="cite_ref-Nation_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He credits Inge for playing "a major role in his intellectual growth."<sup id="cite_ref-Nation_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He graduated from <a href="/wiki/Centennial_High_School_(Compton,_California)" title="Centennial High School (Compton, California)">Centennial High School</a> in 2005 as a straight-A student.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2003.E2.80.932009:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2003–2009:_Career_beginnings">2003–2009: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/C4_(mixtape)" title="C4 (mixtape)">C4 (mixtape)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar_(EP)" title="Kendrick Lamar (EP)">Kendrick Lamar (EP)</a></div>
<p>In 2003, at the age of 16, Lamar released his first full-length project, a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> titled <i>Youngest Head Nigga in Charge (Hub City Threat: Minor of the Year)</i>, under the pseudonym K.Dot.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape was released under Konkrete Jungle Muzik and garnered local recognition for Lamar.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape led to Lamar securing a <a href="/wiki/Recording_contract" title="Recording contract">recording contract</a> with <a href="/wiki/Top_Dawg_Entertainment" title="Top Dawg Entertainment">Top Dawg Entertainment</a> (TDE), a newly founded <a href="/wiki/Independent_record_label" title="Independent record label">independent record label</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Carson,_California" title="Carson, California">Carson, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He began recording material with the label and subsequently released a 26-track mixtape two years later, titled <i>Training Day</i> (2005).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout 2006 and 2007, Lamar would appear alongside other up-and-coming West Coast rappers, such as <a href="/wiki/Jay_Rock" title="Jay Rock">Jay Rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ya_Boy" title="Ya Boy">Ya Boy</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Opening_act" title="Opening act">opening acts</a> for veteran West Coast rapper <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">The Game</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Moniker" class="mw-redirect" title="Moniker">moniker</a> K.Dot, Lamar was also featured on The Game's songs "The Cypha" and "Cali Niggaz".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After receiving a co-sign from Lil Wayne,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Lamar released his third mixtape in 2009, titled <i><a href="/wiki/C4_(mixtape)" title="C4 (mixtape)">C4</a></i>, which was heavily themed around Wayne's album <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Carter_III" title="Tha Carter III">Tha Carter III</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, Lamar decided to no longer go by the stage name of K.Dot and opted to use his birth name. He subsequently released <a href="/wiki/The_Kendrick_Lamar_EP" class="mw-redirect" title="The Kendrick Lamar EP">a self-titled extended play</a> in late 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-dopeboyz1_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dopeboyz1-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> That same year, Lamar along with his TDE label-mates Jay Rock, Ab-Soul and ScHoolboy Q formed <a href="/wiki/Black_Hippy" title="Black Hippy">Black Hippy</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">hip hop supergroup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932011:_Overly_Dedicated_and_Section.80"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2011:_Overly_Dedicated_and_Section.80">2010–2011: <i>Overly Dedicated</i> and <i>Section.80</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Overly_Dedicated" title="Overly Dedicated">Overly Dedicated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Section.80" title="Section.80">Section.80</a></div>
<p>Throughout 2010, Lamar toured with <a href="/wiki/Tech_N9ne" title="Tech N9ne">Tech N9ne</a> and Jay Rock on <i>The Independent Grind</i> tour.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On September 14, 2010, he released the visuals for "P&amp;P 1.5," a song taken from his mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Overly_Dedicated" title="Overly Dedicated">Overly Dedicated</a></i>, featuring his Black Hippy cohort Ab-Soul.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On the same date, Lamar released <i>Overly Dedicated</i> to digital retailers under TDE, and later on September 23, released it for free online.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The project fared well enough to enter the United States <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart, where it peaked at number 72.<sup id="cite_ref-US-R&amp;B-albums_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-R&amp;B-albums-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:KendrickLive.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/KendrickLive.jpg/260px-KendrickLive.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/KendrickLive.jpg/390px-KendrickLive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/KendrickLive.jpg/520px-KendrickLive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="706" data-file-height="351" /></a><figcaption>Lamar performing in Toronto in 2011</figcaption></figure><p>The mixtape includes a song titled "Ignorance Is Bliss", in which Lamar highlights <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> and <a href="/wiki/Street_crime" title="Street crime">street crime</a>, but ends each verse with "ignorance is bliss," giving the message "we know not what we do."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> It was this song specifically that made hip hop producer <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> want to work with Lamar after seeing the music video on YouTube,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> as well as a conversation between Dre and <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>. J Cole helped introduce Lamar to Dre which led to Lamar working with Dr. Dre and <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> on Dre's often-delayed <i><a href="/wiki/Detox_(Dr._Dre_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Detox (Dr. Dre album)">Detox</a></i> album, as well as speculation of Lamar signing to Dr. Dre's record label, <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In December 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> magazine spotlighted Lamar in an edition of their "Indie Intro" series.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2011, Lamar was included in <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)"><i>XXL</i></a>'s annual Top 10 Freshman Class, and was featured on the cover alongside fellow up-and-coming rappers <a href="/wiki/Cyhi_the_Prynce" title="Cyhi the Prynce">Cyhi the Prynce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_the_Godson" title="Fred the Godson">Fred the Godson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mac_Miller" title="Mac Miller">Mac Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yelawolf" title="Yelawolf">Yelawolf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_K.R.I.T." title="Big K.R.I.T.">Big K.R.I.T.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_B" title="Lil B">Lil B</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diggy_Simmons" title="Diggy Simmons">Diggy Simmons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On April 11, 2011, Lamar announced the title of his next full-length project to be <i><a href="/wiki/Section.80" title="Section.80">Section.80</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and the following day the first single "<a href="/wiki/HiiiPoWeR" title="HiiiPoWeR">HiiiPoWeR</a>" was released, the concept of which was to further explain the HiiiPoWeR movement.<sup id="cite_ref-hiiipower_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiiipower-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The song was produced by fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>, marking their first of several collaborations.<sup id="cite_ref-hiiipower_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiiipower-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the topic of whether his next project would be an <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">album</a> or a mixtape, Lamar answered: "I treat every project like it's an album anyway. It's not going to be nothing leftover. I never do nothing like that. These are my leftover songs you all can have them. I'm going to put my best out. My best effort. I'm trying to look for an album in 2012."<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011, Lamar released "Ronald Reagan Era (His Evils)", a cut from <i>Section.80</i>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a> leader <a href="/wiki/RZA" title="RZA">RZA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> On July 2, 2011, Lamar released <i>Section.80</i>, his debut studio album. The album features <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearances</a> from <a href="/wiki/GLC_(rapper)" title="GLC (rapper)">GLC</a>, Colin Munroe, Schoolboy Q, and Ab-Soul, while the production was handled by TDE in-house production team <a href="/wiki/Digi%2BPhonics" title="Digi+Phonics">Digi+Phonics</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Wyldfyer" title="Wyldfyer">Wyldfyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrace_Martin" title="Terrace Martin">Terrace Martin</a> and J. Cole. <i>Section.80</i> went on to sell 5,300 digital copies in its first week, without any television or radio coverage, and received mostly positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2011, while performing at a <a href="/wiki/West_Los_Angeles" title="West Los Angeles">West Los Angeles</a> concert, Lamar was dubbed the "New <a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">King of the West Coast</a>" by Snoop Dogg, Dr. Dre and Game.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On August 24, 2011, Lamar released the music video for the <i>Section.80</i> track, "<a href="/wiki/A.D.H.D_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="A.D.H.D (Kendrick Lamar song)">ADHD</a>". The video was directed by <a href="/wiki/Vashtie_Kola" title="Vashtie Kola">Vashtie Kola</a> who had this to say of the video: "Inspired by "A.D.H.D"'s dark beat and melancholy lyrics which explore a generation in conflict, we find Kendrick Lamar in a video that illustrates the songs[sic] universal and age-old theme of apathetic youth. (...) Shot in New York City during the sweltering July Summer heat".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In October 2011, Lamar appeared alongside fellow American rappers <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, Tech N9ne, <a href="/wiki/MGK_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="MGK (rapper)">MGK</a>, and Big K.R.I.T., in a <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap#Types_of_freestyles" title="Freestyle rap">cypher</a> at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Also in October, Lamar partnered with <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a>, and crafted an original song with producer <a href="/wiki/Nosaj_Thing" title="Nosaj Thing">Nosaj Thing</a> entitled "Cloud 10", to promote <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s new product.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> During 2011, Lamar appeared on several high-profile albums including Game's <i><a href="/wiki/The_R.E.D._Album" title="The R.E.D. Album">The R.E.D. Album</a></i>, Tech N9ne's <i><a href="/wiki/All_6%27s_and_7%27s" title="All 6&#39;s and 7&#39;s">All 6's and 7's</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/9th_Wonder" title="9th Wonder">9th Wonder</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wonder_Years_(9th_Wonder_album)" title="The Wonder Years (9th Wonder album)">The Wonder Years</a></i> and Canadian recording artist <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>-winning <i><a href="/wiki/Take_Care_(album)" title="Take Care (album)">Take Care</a></i>, which featured Lamar on a solo track.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932013:_Good_Kid.2C_M.A.A.D_City_and_controversies"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2013:_Good_Kid,_M.A.A.D_City_and_controversies">2012–2013: <i>Good Kid, M.A.A.D City</i> and controversies</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Good_Kid,_M.A.A.D_City" title="Good Kid, M.A.A.D City">Good Kid, M.A.A.D City</a></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg/250px-Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg/375px-Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg/500px-Kendrick_Lamar_Pitchfork_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>Lamar performing at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Music_Festival" title="Pitchfork Music Festival">Pitchfork Music Festival</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On February 15, 2012, a song by Lamar titled "<a href="/wiki/Cartoon_and_Cereal" title="Cartoon and Cereal">Cartoon and Cereal</a>", featuring fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Gunplay_(rapper)" title="Gunplay (rapper)">Gunplay</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Music_leak" title="Music leak">leaked online</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Lamar later revealed that the track was for his major-label debut studio album and that he had plans to shoot a video for it.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Although the song would later be ranked No. 2 in <a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)"><i>Complex</i></a>'s Best 50 Songs of 2012 list, it would ultimately fail to appear on Lamar's debut.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In February 2012, it was announced that <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fader" title="The Fader">Fader</a></i> had enlisted both Kendrick Lamar and Detroit-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brown_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Danny Brown (rapper)">Danny Brown</a>, to appear on the cover of the magazine's Spring Style issue.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In February, Lamar also embarked on Drake's <a href="/wiki/Club_Paradise_Tour" title="Club Paradise Tour">Club Paradise Tour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opening_act" title="Opening act">opening</a> along with fellow American rappers <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Rocky" title="ASAP Rocky">ASAP Rocky</a> and <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2012, <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> announced that Lamar had signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>, marking the end of his career as an independent artist. Under the new deal, Lamar's projects, including his album <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Kid,_M.A.A.D_City" title="Good Kid, M.A.A.D City">Good Kid, M.A.A.D City</a></i>, would be jointly released via TDE, Aftermath, and Interscope.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Also in March, Lamar appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Call_with_Carson_Daly" title="Last Call with Carson Daly">Last Call with Carson Daly</a></i>, where he spoke on Dr. Dre and his hometown of Compton, California.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On April 2, 2012, Lamar premiered his commercial debut single "<a href="/wiki/The_Recipe_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="The Recipe (Kendrick Lamar song)">The Recipe</a>", on <a href="/wiki/KPWR" title="KPWR">Big Boy's Neighborhood</a> at Power 106. The song, which serves as the first single from <i>Good Kid, M.A.A.D City</i>, was released for digital download the following day. The song was produced by West Coast producer <a href="/wiki/Scoop_DeVille" title="Scoop DeVille">Scoop DeVille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Featuring" class="mw-redirect" title="Featuring">features</a> vocals from his mentor Dr. Dre, who also <a href="/wiki/Audio_mixing_(recorded_music)" title="Audio mixing (recorded music)">mixed</a> the record.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 14, 2012, J. Cole again spoke on his collaborative effort with Lamar. In an interview with Bootleg Kev, Cole stated: "I just started working with Kendrick the other day. We got it in, finally, again. We got maybe four or five [songs] together."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On May 21, Lamar made his <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park</a></i> debut alongside <a href="/wiki/Ace_Hood" title="Ace Hood">Ace Hood</a>, joining <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">Birdman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mack_Maine" title="Mack Maine">Mack Maine</a> on stage to perform "B Boyz". Lamar also talked about his style and sound, Dr. Dre and Snoop Dogg, and his upcoming collaborative LP with J. Cole.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On the same date, Lamar released "War Is My Love", an original song written and recorded for the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_Clancy%27s_Ghost_Recon:_Future_Soldier" title="Tom Clancy&#39;s Ghost Recon: Future Soldier">Tom Clancy's Ghost Recon: Future Soldier</a></i>, for which he appeared in a mini promotional clip earlier that month.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 31, 2012, TDE, Aftermath, and Interscope serviced "<a href="/wiki/Swimming_Pools_(Drank)" title="Swimming Pools (Drank)">Swimming Pools (Drank)</a>" as the lead single from Lamar's debut album. The song's music video, directed by Jerome D, premiered on August 3, 2012, on <i>106 &amp; Park</i>. The song peaked at number 17 on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100">Hot 100</a> in its thirteenth week of gradually climbing up the chart. On August 15, 2012, singer <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> announced via Twitter that both had recorded a song titled "PartyNauseous" for his debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> However, Gaga withdrew from participation in the last moment, citing that it was due to artistic differences and had nothing to do with Lamar.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> On August 17, 2012, Lamar released a song titled "Westside, Right on Time", featuring <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">Southern rapper</a> <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The song was released as part of the "Top Dawg Entertainment Fam Appreciation Week". During 2012, Lamar also toured with the rest of Black Hippy and <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">MMG</a> rapper, <a href="/wiki/Stalley" title="Stalley">Stalley</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a>'s Music Matters Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lamar's major-label debut, <i><a href="/wiki/Good_kid,_m.A.A.d_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Good kid, m.A.A.d city">good kid, m.A.A.d city</a></i>, was released on October 22, 2012. The album debuted at number two in the US, selling 242,100 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-Hits_Daily_Double:_Building_Album_Sales_Chart_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hits_Daily_Double:_Building_Album_Sales_Chart-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, <a href="/wiki/Fuse_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuse TV">Fuse TV</a> listed Lamar's single, "<a href="/wiki/Backseat_Freestyle" title="Backseat Freestyle">Backseat Freestyle</a>" among the top 40 songs of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In a few months' time, the album was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">gold</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA). <a href="/wiki/HipHopDX" title="HipHopDX">HipHopDX</a> named Lamar "Emcee of the Year" for their 2012 Year-End honors.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In November, after Cole posted pictures of himself and Lamar working in the studio, the latter revealed that the two are still working on a project, but an exact release date was not given for the joint album: "We are going to drop that out the sky though. I don't want to give dates. I'm just going to let it fall" in an interview with the LA Leakers.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg/270px-Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg" decoding="async" width="270" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg/405px-Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg/540px-Kendrick-lamar-1360479601.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1068" /></a><figcaption>Lamar performing in 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>On January 26, 2013, Lamar performed the album's first singles "Swimming Pools (Drank)" and "<a href="/wiki/Poetic_Justice_(song)" title="Poetic Justice (song)">Poetic Justice</a>" on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s sketch comedy and variety show, <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>. In the same episode, Lamar also appeared alongside guest host <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a> and comedy band <a href="/wiki/The_Lonely_Island" title="The Lonely Island">The Lonely Island</a>, in an <a href="/wiki/SNL_Digital_Short" title="SNL Digital Short">SNL Digital Short</a>, which spawned the single "<a href="/wiki/YOLO_(The_Lonely_Island_song)" title="YOLO (The Lonely Island song)">YOLO</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-mtvjan22_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvjan22-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> On February 22, 2013, Lamar released the video for "Poetic Justice", the <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a>-sampling collaboration with Canadian rapper Drake.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> On February 26, Lamar performed "Poetic Justice" on the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Just nine months after its release, <i>good kid, m.A.A.d city</i> was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> by the RIAA, Lamar's first platinum certification.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2013, Lamar's verse on the <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a> track "<a href="/wiki/Control_(Big_Sean_song)" title="Control (Big Sean song)">Control</a>", made waves across the hip-hop industry. In the verse, Lamar vows to lyrically "murder" every other up-and-coming rapper, namely J. Cole, <a href="/wiki/Big_K.R.I.T." title="Big K.R.I.T.">Big K.R.I.T.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pusha_T" title="Pusha T">Pusha T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Rocky" title="ASAP Rocky">ASAP Rocky</a>, Drake, Big Sean, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Electronica" title="Jay Electronica">Jay Electronica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_The_Creator" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyler, The Creator">Tyler, The Creator</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mac_Miller" title="Mac Miller">Mac Miller</a>. During the song, Lamar also calls himself the "King of New York", which caused controversy among several New York-based rappers.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Many New York rappers, including <a href="/wiki/Papoose_(rapper)" title="Papoose (rapper)">Papoose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deric_Angelettie" title="Deric Angelettie">The Mad Rapper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Factz" title="Mickey Factz">Mickey Factz</a>, <a href="/wiki/JR_Writer" class="mw-redirect" title="JR Writer">JR Writer</a>, Mysonne, <a href="/wiki/Joell_Ortiz" title="Joell Ortiz">Joell Ortiz</a> and more, took offense to this. Furthermore, fellow American rappers such as Meek Mill, <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassidy_(rapper)" title="Cassidy (rapper)">Cassidy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Budden" title="Joe Budden">Joe Budden</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_L" class="mw-redirect" title="King L">King L</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bizarre_(rapper)" title="Bizarre (rapper)">Bizarre</a> and <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, among many others, released a response or <a href="/wiki/Diss_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Diss track">diss track</a>, within a week.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In the days following the track's release, Lamar's Twitter account saw a 510% increase in followers.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 6, 2013, American recording artist and record producer <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> announced he would be headlining his first solo tour in five years, in support of his sixth album <i><a href="/wiki/Yeezus" title="Yeezus">Yeezus</a></i> (2013), with Kendrick Lamar accompanying him on tour. <a href="/wiki/The_Yeezus_Tour" title="The Yeezus Tour">The Yeezus Tour</a> began in October.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In October, it was also revealed that Lamar would be featured on <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>'s eighth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marshall_Mathers_LP_2" title="The Marshall Mathers LP 2">The Marshall Mathers LP 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On October 15, 2013, Lamar won five awards at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>, including Album of the Year and Lyricist of the Year (the latter of which he had also won the year before).<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> At the award show, Lamar performed "<a href="/wiki/Money_Trees" title="Money Trees">Money Trees</a>", and was also featured in a cypher alongside his Top Dawg label-mates Jay Rock, Schoolboy Q, <a href="/wiki/Isaiah_Rashad" title="Isaiah Rashad">Isaiah Rashad</a>, and Ab-Soul.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> During an October 2013 interview with <i>XXL</i>, Lamar revealed that following The Yeezus Tour, he would begin to start working on his next album.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg/240px-Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg/360px-Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg/480px-Kendrick_Lamar_Yeezus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2035" data-file-height="1525" /></a><figcaption>Lamar performing "<a href="/wiki/Money_Trees" title="Money Trees">Money Trees</a>" during the <a href="/wiki/Yeezus_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Yeezus Tour">Yeezus Tour</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In November 2013, he was named <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "Rapper of the Year", and was featured on the cover of the magazine's "Men of the Year" issue.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> During the interview, he stated that he would begin recording his second major-label studio album in January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Following the issue's release, TDE's <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> Anthony "Top Dawg" Tiffith pulled Lamar from performing at <i>GQ</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s party that accompanies the issue, calling out writer Steve Marsh's profile for its "racial overtones".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <i>GQ</i> editor-in-chief Jim Nelson responded with the following statement: "Kendrick Lamar is one of the most talented new musicians to arrive on the scene in years. That's the reason we chose to celebrate him, wrote an incredibly positive article declaring him the next King of Rap, and gave him our highest honor: putting him on the cover of our Men of the Year issue. I'm not sure how you can spin that into a bad thing, and I encourage anyone interested to read the story and see for themselves."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lamar received a total of seven Grammy nominations at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a> (2014), including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_New_Artist" title="Grammy Award for Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> but did not win in any category. Many publications felt that <a href="/wiki/The_Recording_Academy" title="The Recording Academy">The Recording Academy</a> <a href="/wiki/Snub" title="Snub">snubbed</a> Lamar, as well as <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Macklemore" title="Macklemore">Macklemore</a>, who won <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;category for which Lamar was also nominated.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> At the ceremony, Lamar performed "<a href="/wiki/M.A.A.D_City" title="M.A.A.D City">M.A.A.D City</a>" and a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Radioactive_(Imagine_Dragons_song)" title="Radioactive (Imagine Dragons song)">Radioactive</a>" in a <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mash-up</a> with American rock band <a href="/wiki/Imagine_Dragons" title="Imagine Dragons">Imagine Dragons</a> at the awards ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The remix was again performed by Lamar and the band on February 1, 2014, during the airing of <i>Saturday Night Live</i>, marking Lamar's second appearance on the show.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932016:_To_Pimp_a_Butterfly_and_Untitled_Unmastered"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2016:_To_Pimp_a_Butterfly_and_Untitled_Unmastered">2014–2016: <i>To Pimp a Butterfly</i> and <i>Untitled Unmastered</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/To_Pimp_a_Butterfly" title="To Pimp a Butterfly">To Pimp a Butterfly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Untitled_Unmastered" title="Untitled Unmastered">Untitled Unmastered</a></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kendrick_2015.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Kendrick_2015.jpg/250px-Kendrick_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="206" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Kendrick_2015.jpg/375px-Kendrick_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Kendrick_2015.jpg/500px-Kendrick_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1185" data-file-height="975" /></a><figcaption>Lamar at the Hollywood Palladium during a pre-<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> concert in 2015</figcaption></figure>
<p>In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> in February 2014, Lamar stated he was planning to put out a new album the next September.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> During the same interview, which also included Schoolboy Q, Tiffith, and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Free" title="Dave Free">Dave Free</a>, the possibility of a debut effort from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Hippy" title="Black Hippy">Black Hippy</a> collective appearing in 2014 was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On July 31, 2014, it was announced that Lamar would premiere his short film <i>m.A.A.d</i> at <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance</a>'s inaugural NEXT Fest in Los Angeles on August 9.<sup id="cite_ref-hothip_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hothip-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The film is inspired by <i>good kid, m.A.A.d city</i>, and was directed by Kahlil Joseph, who had previously worked with Lamar on the Yeezus Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-hothip_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hothip-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Lamar featured on the <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> song "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_On_Again" title="It&#39;s On Again">It's On Again</a>", which was written for the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_2" title="The Amazing Spider-Man 2">The Amazing Spider-Man 2</a></i> (2014).<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 23, 2014, Lamar released "<a href="/wiki/I_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="I (Kendrick Lamar song)">i</a>" as the first single from his third album.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> On November 15, 2014, Lamar once again appeared on <i>Saturday Night Live</i> as the musical guest, where he performed "i" and "<a href="/wiki/Pay_for_It_(Jay_Rock_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pay for It (Jay Rock song)">Pay for It</a>", appearing alongside Jay Rock.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Through his appearance, with blackout contacts and his braids partly out, Lamar paid homage to New York-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Method_Man" title="Method Man">Method Man</a>, whose debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Tical_(album)" title="Tical (album)">Tical</a></i> celebrated its 20th anniversary that day.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On December 17, 2014, Lamar debuted a new <a href="/wiki/Untitled_03_%E2%80%93_05.28.2013." title="Untitled 03 – 05.28.2013.">untitled song</a> on one of the final episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">The Colbert Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In early 2015, Lamar won <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance">Best Rap Performance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a> for his song "<a href="/wiki/I_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="I (Kendrick Lamar song)">i</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/57th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="57th Annual Grammy Awards">57th Annual Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> On February 9, 2015, he released his third album's second single, titled "<a href="/wiki/The_Blacker_the_Berry_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Blacker the Berry (Kendrick Lamar song)">The Blacker the Berry</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Originally expected to be released on March 23, 2015, his new album <i><a href="/wiki/To_Pimp_a_Butterfly" title="To Pimp a Butterfly">To Pimp a Butterfly</a></i> was released a week early on March 16, 2015, to rave reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted atop the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart selling 324,000 copies in its first week,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and established <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a>'s global first-day streaming record (9.6&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Lamar was later featured on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, with editor Josh Eells writing he's "arguably the most talented rapper of his generation."<sup id="cite_ref-Eells_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eells-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/181px-Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="181" height="347" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/271px-Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/361px-Kendrick_Lamar_3_F.I.B._2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1143" data-file-height="2193" /></a><figcaption>Lamar in 2016 performing at <a href="/wiki/Festival_Internacional_de_Benic%C3%A0ssim" title="Festival Internacional de Benicàssim">Festival Internacional de Benicàssim</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On May 17, 2015, Lamar featured on the official remix of American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Blood_(Taylor_Swift_song)" title="Bad Blood (Taylor Swift song)">Bad Blood</a>", as well as appearing in the music video.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The original song is in Swift's fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/1989_(Taylor_Swift_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="1989 (Taylor Swift album)">1989</a></i>. The single reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and the music video won them a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Music_Video" title="Grammy Award for Best Music Video">Grammy Award for Best Music Video</a> and a <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> <i>To Pimp a Butterfly</i> produced three other singles with accompanying music videos, "<a href="/wiki/King_Kunta" title="King Kunta">King Kunta</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Alright_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="Alright (Kendrick Lamar song)">Alright</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/These_Walls_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="These Walls (Kendrick Lamar song)">These Walls</a>". The music video for "Alright" received four nominations at the <a href="/wiki/2015_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2015 MTV Video Music Awards">2015 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">Video of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Male_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Male Video">Best Male Video</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-VMA2015_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VMA2015-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The song "<a href="/wiki/For_Free%3F_(Interlude)" title="For Free? (Interlude)">For Free? (Interlude)</a>" also featured a music video,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> as did "<a href="/wiki/U_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="U (Kendrick Lamar song)">u</a>" with "For Sale" as part of the short film "God Is Gangsta".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In October 2015, Lamar announced the Kunta's Groove Sessions Tour, which included eight shows in eight cities.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In early 2016, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> released the track "No More Parties in L.A." on his official <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a>, a collaboration featuring Lamar and produced by West and <a href="/wiki/Madlib" title="Madlib">Madlib</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Lamar also performed a new song, "<a href="/wiki/Untitled_08_%E2%80%93_09.06.2014." title="Untitled 08 – 09.06.2014.">Untitled 2</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i> in January.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> critics commented at the end of the year, "twenty years ago, a conscious rap record wouldn't have penetrated the mainstream in the way Kendrick Lamar did with <i>To Pimp A Butterfly</i>. His sense of timing is impeccable. In the midst of rampant cases of police brutality and racial tension across America, he spews raw, aggressive bars while possibly cutting a rug,"<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_top_albums_2015_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_top_albums_2015-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i> editors noted it "forced critics to think deeply about music. It's an album by the greatest rapper of his generation."<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/Tony_Visconti" title="Tony Visconti">Tony Visconti</a> stated <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Blackstar_(album)" title="Blackstar (album)">Blackstar</a></i> (2016) was influenced by Lamar's work, "we were listening to a lot of Kendrick Lamar [...] we loved the fact Kendrick was so open-minded and he didn't do a straight-up hip-hop record. He threw everything on there, and that's exactly what we wanted to do."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Visconti also stated this about Lamar while talking about "rule-breakers" in music. </p><blockquote><p>"His album <i>To Pimp A Butterfly</i> broke every rule in the book and he had a number one album glued to the top of the charts. You'd think certain labels would learn from that. But they take somebody who is out there and say, 'That's what people want.' No, people want that for one week. You don't want the same song every single day of your life."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>Lamar won five Grammys at the <a href="/wiki/58th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="58th Annual Grammy Awards">58th ceremony</a>, including Best Rap Album for <i>To Pimp a Butterfly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-grammys16_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammys16-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Other nominations included Album of the Year and Song of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-grammys16noms_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammys16noms-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> At the ceremony, Lamar performed a medley of "<a href="/wiki/The_Blacker_the_Berry_(song)" title="The Blacker the Berry (song)">The Blacker the Berry</a>" and "Alright".<sup id="cite_ref-auto_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> called it the best moment of the night,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> with the latter writing "It was easily one of the best live TV performances in history."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 4, 2016, Lamar released a compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Untitled_Unmastered" title="Untitled Unmastered">Untitled Unmastered</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> containing eight untitled tracks, each dated.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The tracks were unfinished <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demos</a> from the recording of <i>To Pimp a Butterfly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The compilation album debuted atop the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.932018:_Damn.2C_Black_Panther_soundtrack_and_hiatus"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–2018:_Damn,_Black_Panther_soundtrack_and_hiatus">2017–2018: <i>Damn</i>, <i>Black Panther</i> soundtrack and hiatus</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Damn_(Kendrick_Lamar_album)" title="Damn (Kendrick Lamar album)">Damn (Kendrick Lamar album)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(soundtrack)" title="Black Panther (soundtrack)">Black Panther (soundtrack)</a></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_@_TD_Garden_(Boston,_MA)_(36059988466).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_%40_TD_Garden_%28Boston%2C_MA%29_%2836059988466%29.jpg/250px-Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_%40_TD_Garden_%28Boston%2C_MA%29_%2836059988466%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_%40_TD_Garden_%28Boston%2C_MA%29_%2836059988466%29.jpg/375px-Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_%40_TD_Garden_%28Boston%2C_MA%29_%2836059988466%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_%40_TD_Garden_%28Boston%2C_MA%29_%2836059988466%29.jpg/500px-Kendrick_Lamar-_The_DAMN._Tour_%40_TD_Garden_%28Boston%2C_MA%29_%2836059988466%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5790" data-file-height="3860" /></a><figcaption>Lamar on <a href="/wiki/The_Damn_Tour" title="The Damn Tour">The Damn Tour</a> in 2017</figcaption></figure>
<p>On March 23, 2017, Lamar released a promotional single "<a href="/wiki/The_Heart_Part_4" title="The Heart Part 4">The Heart Part 4</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> A week later, Lamar released the lead single, titled "<a href="/wiki/Humble_(song)" title="Humble (song)">Humble</a>", accompanied by its music video.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On April 7, 2017, his fourth studio album was made available for pre-order and confirmed to be released on April 14, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-vlad4th_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vlad4th-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LATimes-Apr7_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-Apr7-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> On April 11, Lamar announced the album title, <i><a href="/wiki/Damn_(Kendrick_Lamar_album)" title="Damn (Kendrick Lamar album)">Damn</a></i> (stylized as <i>DAMN.</i>), as well as the track list, which confirmed guest appearances by <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, Zacari, and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The album was released on April 14, 2017, to rave reviews, with a <i>Rolling Stone</i> writer describing it as a combination of "the old school and the next-level."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> It marked his third number one album on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, and the single "Humble" became his first number one as a lead artist on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> On May 4, 2017, <i>Damn</i> was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Lamar later released the <i>DAMN.</i> Collectors Edition in mid-December 2017, with the tracklist from the original album in reverse order.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Along with Tiffith, Lamar produced and curated the film soundtrack for the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a> superhero film <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(film)" title="Black Panther (film)">Black Panther</a></i> (2018), titled <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(soundtrack)" title="Black Panther (soundtrack)">Black Panther: The Album</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Panther_Soundtrack_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Panther_Soundtrack-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> A single from the soundtrack, "<a href="/wiki/All_the_Stars" title="All the Stars">All the Stars</a>", was released in January 2018 featuring singer <a href="/wiki/SZA_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="SZA (singer)">SZA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Panther_Soundtrack_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Panther_Soundtrack-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and it earned him an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, another track, titled "<a href="/wiki/King%27s_Dead" title="King&#39;s Dead">King's Dead</a>", was released by <a href="/wiki/Jay_Rock" title="Jay Rock">Jay Rock</a> featuring Lamar, <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Blake_(musician)" title="James Blake (musician)">James Blake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The third single, "<a href="/wiki/Pray_for_Me_(The_Weeknd_and_Kendrick_Lamar_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pray for Me (The Weeknd and Kendrick Lamar song)">Pray For Me</a>", by Lamar and <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">The Weeknd</a>, was released in February 2018, ahead of the album's release in that month.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(soundtrack)" title="Black Panther (soundtrack)">Black Panther: The Album</a></i> was released on February 9, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018, Lamar's song publishing deal with <a href="/wiki/Warner_Chappell_Music" title="Warner Chappell Music">Warner Chappell Music</a> began to expire; TDE was seeking $20 to $40 million for the rapper's catalogue.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Lamar opened the <a href="/wiki/60th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="60th Annual Grammy Awards">60th Annual Grammy Awards</a> with a medley of "XXX", "Lust", "DNA", "Humble", "King's Dead" and <a href="/wiki/Rich_the_Kid" title="Rich the Kid">Rich the Kid</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/New_Freezer" title="New Freezer">New Freezer</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> He was also nominated for seven awards, including Album of the Year and Best Rap Album for <i>Damn</i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a>, Best Rap Performance, Best Rap Song, and Best Music Video for "Humble", and Best Rap/Sung Performance for "<a href="/wiki/Loyalty_(Kendrick_Lamar_song)" title="Loyalty (Kendrick Lamar song)">Loyalty</a>" with Rihanna. Lamar ultimately won five awards at the ceremony, for Best Rap Album, Best Rap Performance, Best Rap Song, Best Music Video, and Best Rap/Sung Performance.<sup id="cite_ref-damn_grammys_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-damn_grammys-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> After the <i>Black Panther</i> soundtrack, Lamar did not release music of his own for four years.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2020.E2.80.93present:_PGLang_and_Mr._Morale_.26_the_Big_Steppers"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–present:_PGLang_and_Mr._Morale_&amp;_the_Big_Steppers">2020–present: PGLang and <i>Mr. Morale &amp; the Big Steppers</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/PGLang" title="PGLang">PGLang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mr._Morale_%26_the_Big_Steppers" title="Mr. Morale &amp; the Big Steppers">Mr. Morale &amp; the Big Steppers</a></div>
<p>On March 5, 2020, Lamar and Free launched <a href="/wiki/PGLang" title="PGLang">PGLang</a>, which was described as a multilingual, artist-friendly service company.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> In a press release, Free claimed that the company "is not a record label, a movie studio, or a publishing house. This is something new. In this overstimulated time, we are focused on cultivating raw expression from grassroots partnerships."<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The announcement also featured a "visual mission statement", a four-minute short film starring Lamar, <a href="/wiki/Baby_Keem" title="Baby Keem">Baby Keem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorja_Smith" title="Jorja Smith">Jorja Smith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yara_Shahidi" title="Yara Shahidi">Yara Shahidi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 20, 2021, Lamar announced on a blog post that he was in the middle of producing his final album under TDE.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he appeared on Baby Keem's single "<a href="/wiki/Family_Ties_(song)" title="Family Ties (song)">Family Ties</a>", from his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Melodic_Blue" title="The Melodic Blue">The Melodic Blue</a></i>. The song marked Lamar's first single release in three years, and won Best Rap Performance at the <a href="/wiki/64th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="64th Annual Grammy Awards">64th Annual Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Lamar additionally made several appearances on <i>The Melodic Blue</i>, on the tracks "<a href="/wiki/Range_Brothers" title="Range Brothers">Range Brothers</a>" and "Vent". On November 12, Lamar made his comeback performance by headlining the first night of Day N Vegas.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 13, 2022, Lamar headlined the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LVI halftime show">Super Bowl LVI halftime show</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, which won him the <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Variety_Special_(Live)" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Variety Special (Live)">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Variety Special (Live)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> On May 8, he released the promotional single "<a href="/wiki/The_Heart_Part_5" title="The Heart Part 5">The Heart Part 5</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Lamar's fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Morale_%26_the_Big_Steppers" title="Mr. Morale &amp;
